    <li> I had bought the bigger and more expensive trimmer they make, the one that is digital. All we had was troubles! It had so many glitches and we wanted to be able to turn it on and just use it! My husband uses it on his face and neck and I use it on the back of his neck during hair cuts. Fantastic for both. When we had the more expensive ones you couldn&#x27;t use it when it was plugged in, but this one will. Which is a nice feature in case you need a quick trim and forgot to charge it. The charge lasts for many many hours once it&#x27;s charged and charging isn&#x27;t that long. We took the bigger and better one back to the store, got our money back, came on here and purchased two of these instantly. The first one we ever bought lasted us around 8 years and would have gone longer but I dropped it just right (I had dropped it many times in the past with no issues) and it landed in a way that bent the hinge and it wouldn&#x27;t close anymore.     <li> It does the job well, but it&#x27;s pretty ridiculous that it can&#x27;t run off the outlet. What I mean is that if the battery runs out, you have to charge it.     <li> Old generation nicad battery with memory problem. Battery soldered in, not meant to be changed as they want you to replace entire product. If your battery no longer holds a charge you can take it to Batteries Plus and have them install a new generation nicad battery without the memory problem.  They charge about $25.  Consult youtube for demonstration of battery replacement. Length adjuster locks into place well.  Tines don&#x27;t depress when pressure applied as bad as most other shavers that I have tried.  Have had no issues with pulling hair.  Would have given 3 stars (meaning: what you expect for what you pay) if the battery wasn&#x27;t garbage.</li>
    <li> I bought the predecessor to this beard trimmer more than three years ago, and loved it. After carelessly dropping my old one I broke it, and am back for another.     Pros:     * Scrolling wheel height adjustment.   ----&gt; A very nice feature, the height holds well, unlike some trimmers. You can use pressure against your face and it won&#x27;t retreat to a shorter height setting that creates a thin spot.   ----&gt; After only two or three times, you will know how high you want it. For example, I always trim my beard on a \\&quot;6\\&quot; and my mustache on a \\&quot;4\\&quot;     * Removable head to trim beard edges.     * Strong motor/ blades provide pain-free trim.     * Holds its charge for a long time. (I charge it full before I travel, and don&#x27;t even bother packing the charger, because I trust it to function the whole week.)     * Shaver head lifts easily to remove stray hair that gets into the motor area.     * Cordless -&gt; To avoid having to clean the bathroom after a big trim, (If I didn&#x27;t trim for a week or so) I will take it in the back yard and set it 1 setting higher (\\&quot;7\\&quot; instead of \\&quot;6\\&quot;). Then I give it a quick hit to get rid of the long hair, and then return to the bathroom to finish the detail work.       Cons:     * It will need a place to lay flat, or a pouch to hang in. It doesn&#x27;t stand on end, and the charger unit plugs into the base (at the bottom end of the demo picture).     * I did mention I broke my old one. I had removed the height guard, and was emptying the hair from under the shaver head. The pivot is plastic, and while I had it open, I dropped the shaver. It landed head down (of course) and the pivot broke. Totally user error, but it is a weak spot.       ----------     Final Thoughts:     I love this thing. It provides a quick clean trim. I would say that it usually takes no less than 3 minutes for a quick trim, maybe as long as 8-10 minutes if I am going to detail the edges after a month of quick trims.     I highlighted some cons for a fair review, but I have nothing against this razor. It trimmed well for three years, and was still holding a charge for weeks when I broke it.     (I liked it even more after trying the [[ASIN:B000BI3PYE Remington PG350 Precision Deluxe Rechargeable Personal Grooming Kit]]. I bought that quick because I needed a trim, and it confirmed how well this razor worked, and shaped my thoughts for this review. To compare to a bad item, check my review of that item.)</li>
    <li> I retract my primarily favorable review that I wrote after using the trimmer a couple of times.  In the 5th month I was unable to locate the recharger (it uses an unconventional pin that inserts into the base of the trimmer).  I finally located it, and it&#x27;s apparently been charging (i.e., the green light is on) for two days.  However, to no effect.  The unit is completely dead.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is a shaver available at a number of places on the internet at prices ranging from $15 to $60.  Since I didn&#x27;t play the latter for it, I&#x27;m disinclined to go to the bother and time of having it repaired.  It was wasted money.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Even though the Remington is more precise that the Panasonic it replaces, the Panasonic had an ingenious rechargable plug that jack-knifed open from the base, permitting the entire shaver to be inserted in the AC and ensuring against loss of AC connection.  I would look for either that feature or go with regular battery-operated (a permanently connected electrical cord is also worth considering).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Obviously, I got a lemon, or a bad charger.  Nevertheless, best not to spend more than $10 on these and to regard them as disposable--more potentially irritating gadgetry in our cluttered lives.</li>
    <li> Great value for a rechargeable trimmer.  Loads of functions,  several attachments and had to buy one for each son.  Thanks Remington.</li>
    <li> Works great. Lots of length options. battery life has been good.</li>
    <li> A dry cell trimmer I once had for travel was a joke, so I needed convincing.  After much research, I chose the Remington for a two week trip in Japan.  It may well replace my hardwired, motor-driven home clipper.  My current persona is hair and beard at about 1/8 inch (Remington setting #3), and the stability and solidness of the adjustment are superb.  I trim about every four days, but I have touched-up after two days and was amazed at how much infinitesimally short hair it gets:  Really reliable adjustment.  I run it, plugged in, for about ten minutes at a time, and the only oddity is fluctuation of speed toward the end:  Probably the charging cycle, but it doesn&#x27;t seem to affect performance.  It is easy to clean, and lubrication-free is a real plus.  This was a very sound purchase.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve owned the previous model of the trimmer and I loved it. This one is even better.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;m very happy with this item; it is exactly what I wanted and works quite well</li>
    <li> This trimmer does the job great. I use it to keep my goatee well-groomed and it does the job very well. I wish the lower number settings had finer adjustments between them, but this is a problem I have with any trimmers. Other than that, this trimmer is a great bargain. It does the job just as well as much more pricey trimmers. It is easy to clean and maintain, seems to keep cutting well over time, and gives a nice even trim.     <li> I have a beard, so I need something reliable to keep it evenly trimmed. I wouldn&#x27;t go with any other trimmer besides the Remington MB-200.  The razor length is adjustable to nine different lengths with a simple scrolling wheel, so you can cut your beard and body hair down to any length you want. The blades are titanium coated, so they&#x27;ll last long and there&#x27;s no need to sharpen them. Cleaning is easy, too. The top opens up, and you simply blow or shake the hair out. Charging is a cinch; just plug it in and let it charge, and a charging indicator lets you know when it&#x27;s finished charging.   It seems that a lot of people are complaining about the life span of the razor&#x27;s rechargeable battery. I&#x27;m thinking some people might have faulty razors, but this is my second one and I&#x27;m happy with the battery life. When it&#x27;s new you should get a few uses out of it before you have to charge it again. Like with any rechargeable device, you should only charge it when the battery is running low for maximum battery life. After a year or so of regular use, you&#x27;ll notice that you have to charge it a bit more frequently, but this is the case with all rechargable devices, so it&#x27;s not that big of a deal.  My only real complaint with the MB-200 is that the hinge that allows you to clean inside of the razor is plastic. It shouldn&#x27;t break if you&#x27;re careful with it, so just don&#x27;t drop it repeatedly. Otherwise, the fact that it&#x27;s plastic isn&#x27;t that big of a deal, and it helps keep the cost way down. I first had an older version of the MB-200, and it lasted a few years (until Feb. 2011) until I dropped it on my bathroom floor, breaking one of the plastic hinges and one of the teeth on the comb.  I should also mention that this isn&#x27;t an electric/corded trimmer; it&#x27;s cordless. For the best performance, you have to charge it fully before unplugging it and using it.  The bottom line: If you&#x27;re in the market for a rechargeable, reliable, fairly sturdy beard/body hair trimmer, then go with the Remington MB-200. I&#x27;ve had mine for almost six months now, and the battery is more or less as good as it was when I first opened it. It gives me a clean, even trim every time, and cleaning is easy. And for under $20, I promise you won&#x27;t go wrong!</li>

I don&#x27;t want to trim my ears with it, and it won&#x27;t do it, unless I was crazy enough to stick the corner in my ear and chop half my ear off. It holds a charge for a good long time, is neat, and sharp. I don&#x27;t know what else you could ask for a trimmer, except to get it half off - and, oh yeah, it did that too!    I highly recommend this over the Phillips Norelco G370 which I had before. I lost chargers, the stand that comes with the shaver doesn&#x27;t really allow for charging in place.. it was just a mess.     <li> I had an MB300 for about a year (which is the exact same thing as the MB200 with the addition of a useless mini trimmer) but a piece of a metal spring inside the top of the unit where you open to empty trimmings rusted and broke, rendering it useless and unrepairable.  I guess I managed to get enough water in there while in the bathroom on occasion for it to rust out.  I really wish that spring was made out of stainless steel.    I purchased this MB200 a month ago to replace my broken MB300 after reading several atrocious reviews on competing products, and after having several failures and returns of other models including Norelco.  I have tried many beard trimmers over the years for both trimming stubble on my face and cutting my own hair, and this easily beats them all (I prefer the rechargeable ones with adjustable combs).  Some of the competing products are made out of cheap plastic and the fins on the combs have broken (specifically Norelco), some have too little cutting power, on some the blades on some are not wide enough, and others are just designed by moron engineers.      The MB200 has decent power, the cutting blade is reasonably wide, and the adjustment mechanism for the comb is well designed so you don&#x27;t accidentally choose the wrong length or have it end up moving around on you and ending up with a shaved spot where you didn&#x27;t mean to.  I&#x27;m not unhappy with the choice of Ni-Cd batteries since they last a reasonable amount of time, and I&#x27;m guessing that Lithium-Ion would have put it at a price point that would be non-competitive.   I do wish the batteries weren&#x27;t soldered in so it would be easier to replace them.  Seeing that this is the only decent rechargeable trimmer out there, I am going to purchase a couple more of these - one for my travel bag, and another as a spare.  These days companies seem to revise well designed products, and forget everything they learned that was good about the previous designs.  I hope Remington keeps the person/team around that designed this, keeps this model around for a long time to come,   and hopefully makes it a little mode water resistant and upgrades that spring inside to stainless steel!</li>

Also, if you&#x27;re like me, beard trimmers can get annoying pretty quickly. Just consider all the separate parts that usually come with beard trimmers - my last one had a stand for the 7 different guards, plus the oil and the comb! Alternatively, this trimmer&#x27;s zoom wheel is a great alternative to the usual method of swapping out edge guards. The trimmer comes with no stand, no separate edge guards, nor any oil. Instead, it contains only one detachable guard (works great with the zoom wheel, allowing 9 different lengths), one small comb, and the electric cord. Plus, it never needs to be oiled! (And everything stores away without any hassle!)  Overall this was a great purchase. There are probably other trimmers out there that have even longer battery lives, have even more power, or cut even closer*, but for the money, this was an exceptional purchase.     <li> I was about to shave my beard off about two months ago having been feed up with keeping it trim.  I used a trimmer intended for hair cutting and it did not work well at all, especially the incessant hair pulls.  I noticed this trimmer on Amazon and its good reviews, so I ordered one. I especially like the height adjustment mechanism.  I&#x27;ve yet needed to recharge it over those two months.  I wish it had a charge indicator but nevertheless, given the results, I highly recommend it and have to rate it 5 stars.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update#1: as of today 11/14/2011 the Remington trimmer is still going strong with performance as good as on day one.  I wouldn&#x27;t change a thing in my review of this trimmer except to add longevity to its attributes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update#2: as of today 11/01/2013 the Remington Trimmer is still working fine after all these years of use, albeit, I get fewer \\&quot;trims\\&quot; per charge and needs to be charged more frequently. I believe the secret for the batteries longevity is to resist charging it after every use and charge it only when it is completely discharged (almost fully depleted).  These NiCad batteries have what is known as a \\&quot;memory effect\\&quot; and if you continually charge it before it is completely discharged, this will effectively lower the amount of charge it can hold (short answer to long explanation of this effect).  Also, overcharging by leaving it on the charger too long,  will also cause it to discharge quickly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update#3: as of today 06/01/2014 as expected, my trimmer is slowly going south. I now can only get two full trims per charge.  I fully expect it to get worse quickly now. When I&#x27;m down to one trim per charge, I may take it apart and try to solder in new NiCad&#x27;s if the ones in the trimmer are the standard AA size.  If that proves too complicated or time consuming, I&#x27;ll spring for a new one.  I&#x27;ll try to remember to post the results here in another update.  I know it&#x27;s not cost effective to try to repair it, but my curiosity will get the best of me and the trimmer itself, still does a good job on my beard and mustache.</li>

    <li> Works very well for trimming beards to 9 lengths including a close stubble look. The down side is the battery, NiCD, which suffers from memory effect if improperly charged. If you find a trimmer for about the same price with Lithium or NiMH batteries then get that since they are fool-proof to charge. If you&#x27;re willing to put up with properly charging this and the price is right, you&#x27;ll be happy with this one. Like I said it performs very well.  NiCD batteries should be fully drained before charging, and fully charged before using; otherwise the battery life will shorten and if done a number of times the battery will stop holding a charge. (I&#x27;m guessing reviewers who say the battery stops working after a couple weeks didn&#x27;t do this) Also during use, NiCD batteries provide steady power until they run out suddenly with little warning. The problem with that is the charge time is 14 to 16 hours, which means even if you use the trimmer the night before, if the battery dies you can&#x27;t finish the job in the morning without fear of shortening the life of the battery somewhat.  But overall it performs very well and if charged properly should work for years and is very cheap; so I only took off 1 star.</li>

I have been careful and haven&#x27;t had any problems, but I can see that a bit too much force will snap it off. Be careful and you will be fine, but don&#x27;t let your kids play with it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In summary: very good lightweigt rechargeable trimmer. Don&#x27;t bring it anywhere near water, but still cleanable. I even use it on other...areas of my body with great results.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;EDIT: Had to knock it down a star for battery life. When you charge it, it definitely has enough juice to trim whatever you need to.     <li> Before you purchase this beard trimmer, be aware of these two major flaws:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1.  It ONLY runs on battery power.  Everyone nowadays is accustomed to using their laptop and cell phone, where you can take your device with a dead battery, plug it in, and begin using it right away with full power.  With this beard trimmer, you can&#x27;t just plug it in and use it-- the battery has to charge first.  If your trimmer is new, that takes at least a few hours.  As your device gets older, it takes longer and longer--it now takes me a full 24 hours to charge the battery to the point where I can get a full beard-trim out of it.  And that brings me to flaw #2.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2.  The battery will stop holding a charge after a fairly short life.  I used mine about once a week for about three years before it got really bad-- that&#x27;s probably 100-150 charges of the battery.  If you&#x27;re someone using it every day, of course you would go through 100-150 charges much faster.  As I mentioned, I now need to charge the trimmer for about 24 hours before I can use it.  As soon as it gets unplugged, it will lose the entire charge within about 6 hours or so whether it is turned on or not.  Thus, I have to plan my beard trimming 24 hours in advance, and for someone with a hectic life this can be very difficult.  I don&#x27;t think there&#x27;s any way to swap out the battery for a new one--I have done some searching for solutions and have not found anything.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If there was a way to swap out the battery for a new one I would do it, because I otherwise like this beard trimmer. Having experienced with rechargeable devices with cheap rechargeable batteries, I decided to open it up to see if I could replace the batteries.  I discovered that the batteries are permanently mounted and not replaceable, unless you want to do some work to disconnect the old batteries and solder 2 replacement AA-size batteries into place.  Each of the original batteries is rated 600mA.  Hence, this was a practically made to be a disposable trimmer.  Its life probably is dependent on how often you use it and how you recharge it.  Frankly, it is unfortunate that it was engineered to the thrown away before the blades become dull. The charge times would be shorter and the run times would be longer, and the shaver would be much more eco-friendly.  Because let&#x27;s face it, are most people going to take their trimmer to a battery recycling facility or a Batteries Plus when their trimmer dies after 3 months? UPDATE: Remington customer service reached out and after validating my purchase, mailed me a replacement device which arrived today (10/30/2014). It&#x27;s great to see them stand by their product and replace devices like this (note that there is a 2-year warranty on these units). While the support is great, I&#x27;m leaving my original review intact since the type of battery used in the device, Nickel-Cadmium, does not appear to have changed which means it will also likely die in after a year and a half of use. Maybe my first device was a from  a bad batch (not likely after seeing the other reviews), but in general Nickel-Cadmium batteries don&#x27;t have as good a shelf-life as Lithium-Ion batteries. If this model were updated with a Lithium-Ion battery it would be a no-brainer purchase and recommendation, even if it added $20 to the cost.     Again, great to see them stand by their warranty and replace a bad battery. I&#x27;ll try and remember to update this review a few months down the road to share how this battery holds up.</li>

This means if you leave your trimmer unplugged for any significant length of time (more than about a day), the battery loses its charge. It then takes a really long time to recharge. I just leave my trimmer plugged in in a corner of the room at all times so that I don&#x27;t worry about it not being charged when I need it&lt;br /&gt;- If the battery is dead, you cannot operate the trimmer by plugging it in. This is not how things should work. If your cell phone battery dies, you can plug your phone in and turn it on as long as it&#x27;s connected to the power outlet. With the trimmer, you have to wait until the battery recharges, then use battery power. And the battery takes a LONG time to recharge (more than a couple hours)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also, some people like trimmers that can stand up. This one cannot stand, but must lie flat.     <li> I bought this product as a gift.  It came highly recommended.  The receiver is very pleased and now looks ever so handsome.&lt;br /&gt;Thanks.</li>
    <li> (IMPORTANT NOTES: I use only setting \\&quot;1\\&quot; - I prefer a &#x60;scruff&#x27; look and generally do not grow a full beard, so please keep this in mind when reading my review.  I have not used any of the longer settings)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My review will consist of 3 parts - first, a review of the Remington&#x27;s performance and, second, some tips &amp; tricks I have figured out when using the Remington.  Lastly, some final thoughts / comments.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;PERFORMANCE&lt;br /&gt;I have owned the Remington for about 3 months now and am generally pleased with its performance.  The product is 100% analog - there are no digital displays and the length is adjusted via manual \\&quot;zoom wheel.\\&quot;  Some trimmers indicate length via a digital display screen.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The trimmer has a total of 9 length settings.  It can go as low as 1.5mm (that&#x27;s the setting I use 100% of the time) and as long as 18mm (setting # 9).  The zoom wheel is placed exactly where I happen to place my thumb during shaving.  This hasn&#x27;t presented much of a problem, at least not for me - but I can see where it might for some people.  On setting 1 (1.5mm), the trimmer will give a *slightly* longer than 5-o&#x27;clock shadow look - more of a &#x60;scruff&#x27; look (if that makes sense), but it&#x27;s pretty darn short (the way I like it).  I tend to press the unit pretty firmly against my face on some parts.  The guide comb seems to do an admirable job of preventing nicks / scrapes / and cuts - I have not experienced any problems of the sort.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The unit itself is fairly ergonomic and easy to hold.  It feels like a natural extension of my hand and fits snugly in my palm - almost like a fork or a spoon.  I do not have any issues with the unit slipping in undesired positions, etc.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The blade area is approximately 1.5 inches wide - which seems to be &#x60;just right.&#x27; (see my picture)  It&#x27;s not too narrow, and not too wide. It seems to hug my face accurately and efficiently trims facial hair.  I have a fairly chiseled face - not sure if that matters.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The length guide comb is removable - you simply just need to yank it off (see my picture).  This serves two purposes.  First, it enables the user to use the unit to trim facial &#x60;borders&#x27; at the edge of one&#x27;s beard.  Personally, I just stick to my foil shaver for that, so I cannot comment on how well the Remington might perform (never have used that feature).  Secondly, the blades themselves can be flipped open to enable cleaning inside the trimmer&#x27;s cavity where some hair might collect over time (see my picture).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The unit comes with a standard plug-in wall charger and a cleaning brush.  During charging, a green light remains lit.  Unfortunately, the unit does not indicate remaining battery life.  This would have been a nice feature, though really it is a minor gripe on my end.  Some have complained about the unit&#x27;s lack of battery life.  For me this has not been an issue.  I seem to be able to use the trimmer for several shavings before charging becomes an issue.  As well, 100% of my shaving is done in my home and so it&#x27;s just as easy for me to charge the unit - I do not travel with it.  I don&#x27;t necessarily disagree with other reviews that complain about battery life - it just hasn&#x27;t been a problem for me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It also would have been nice to have some sort of cloth carrying pouch for the trimmer.  In all fairness, most of these trimmers seem not to include this - so it&#x27;s not a deal breaker in my book.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;TIPS &amp; TRICKS&lt;br /&gt;Like any type of facial hair trimming product, your face will take time, perhaps several weeks, to &#x60;adjust&#x27; to the shaver&#x27;s surface area.  This is a known fact among the industry and, in fact, many regular / foil shavers will indicate this in the product&#x27;s user guide.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As far as usage, you may need to use a variety of angles and techniques on different parts of your face whilst trimming your facial hair.  For me, on some parts of my face, I trim against the direction of the facial hair (left-hand side ofmy face), but on my right-hand side, I tend to use a combination of a &#x60;swirling&#x27; motion to trim my hair along with cutting crosswise.  On my chin, I tend to use a quick, firm, and repeated upward motion.  For whatever reason, these all seem to work well.  I figured out these methods after having the trimmer for a few weeks and just seemed to fall into place over time.  If you look closely, you will see that the hair on your face does not grow uniformly - some parts grow in different directions than other parts of your face.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For those who prefer to maintain the scruff appearance, you will definitely need to trim your face more than once a day.  I do so twice - once in the morning before work, and also shortly before I go to bed.  I suppose this is not unique to the Remington, but just a general observation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;FINAL THOUGHTS / COMMENTS&lt;br /&gt;Generally speaking, I am satisfied with the product.  I do not see myself running out and buying another brand - this one more than suffices.  The unit is simple and 100% analog (to me that is a plus).  Electronic components can wear over time or simply malfunction.  I guess I tend to be a bit more &#x60;old school&#x27; in that regard (but feel free to disagree).  The price point is also very affordable.</li>
    <li> My husband used this trimmer for years before his went out. He was so disappointed that he couldn&#x27;t find another in store, and was thrilled when we found it online. He loves it! He has very thick, coarse facial hair and is extremely particular.</li>
